=520  \\$aLorenz Mizler took his degree in music in 1736 at the University of Leipzig, where he lectured on music history ('Die gelehrte Historie der Musik'), mathematics, and philosophy. Aiming to “confer on music the shape of a science," Mizler lay at the basis of the development of 'Musikwissenschaft'. He was closely connected to Christian Wolff and Johann Mattheson.
=534  \\$aVol. 1 was originally published in 1736-39, vol. 2 in 1740-43, vol. 3 in 1746-52, and vol. 4 in 1754.

=500  \\$aAmédée Reuchsel was a French composer and organist. He studied music at the Conservatories of Brussels and Paris; in the latter he had as teacher in composition the master Gabriel Fauré. He obtained the position of organist of the church of Saint Dionysus in Paris and in 1908 he was awarded the Chartier prize for chamber music. His father Léon (1840-1915) was also a musician, as were his brother Maurice (1880-1968) and his son Eugène (1900-1988).

=041  \\$adut$afre$aita$alat
=100  \\$4aut$aHuygens, Constantijn$d1596-1687$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q560746$95174
=245  \\$aHarders-klachte
=246  \1$aThirsis op de doodt van sine Phyllis door Ysbraeck om-gekomen.
=300  \\$a[3] pages
=500  \\$aPoems in Dutch, Latin, French and Italian version, all written in 1620
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Kerkuraia mastix', 'Batava Tempe' and 'Groete aen de ioffrouwen'
=520  \\$aIn early January 1620, Maria van Mathenesse fell under the eyes of her fiancé, Jacob van Wassenaar, Lord of Warmond, near Leiden, through the ice and drowned. The English envoy Carleton describes this tragic event in a letter of 14 January 1620. On request from the same Carleton, Huygens writes, as mentioned to Daniel Heinsius, this sad four-part work Ter aóax vovvov (four tears). Huygens was inspired for this sad poem by the first idyll of Theocritus: 'Thirsis' lament for the death of Dafnis'. He probably knew Heinsius' edition of it. Perhaps that is the reason why Huygens is extra curious about Heinsius' opinion of these poems. The Haarlem priest Joan Albert Ban (1597–1644) composed emotive music for this poem.
=590  \\$aop den selven sin. In de welcke Thirsis vertoont dennHeere van Warmon, beclaghende het drouvich ongeval, sine Bruyd (wijlen dochter van den Heere van Matenes, Heere van Haserwoude) door Ys-braecke over-ghecomen

=010  \\$a 
=020  \\$a9781107004283
=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aRose, Stephen$4aut$922246
=245  14$aThe Musician in Literature in the Age of Bach
=260  \\$aCambridge$bCambridge University Press$c2011
=300  \\$aix-237 pages
=520  \\$a"Using novels and autobiographies from Bach's Germany, Stephen Rose suggests new ways of interpreting the lives and social status of musicians. The study focuses on satirical novels written by musicians that describe the lives of performers and composers, as well as the autobiographies of Bach's contemporaries. These narratives represent musicians variously as picaresque outcasts, honourable craft-workers, foolish bunglers and respected virtuosos. They probe the lives of musicians considered taboo or aberrant in the period, such as street entertainers and Italian castratos. The novels and autobiographies also reveal two major debates that shaped the mindset and social identity of musicians: was music a sensual or rational craft, and should musicians integrate within society or be regarded as outsiders? Quoting from an array of little-known novels, this book shows how an interdisciplinary approach can transform our understanding of Bach and his contemporaries"$cProvided by publisher.

=245  \\$aAlbum Agatha Home Drummond
=500  \\$aCollection of keyboard music belonging to Agatha Home Drummond.
Written index on first page lists 19 items, the last two have been removed from this collection. 
=500  \\$aAgatha Home Drummond might have lived in Edinburgh as most of the music seems to come from Edinburgh music sellers and publishers. 
=501  \\$aa.	Natale Corri, Three Sonatas, for the Piano Forte or Harpsichord with an accompanyment for a violin Op.1 (33)
b.	Domenico Corri, Three Sonatas for the Harpsichord or Piano Forte op.5 [114-135] (22)
c.	Mazzinghi, Overture Virginia (Number of the Opera Overtures adapted for the Harpsichord or Piano Forte with an Acc. for a Violin) (8)
d.	Reeve, The Favorite Overture to the popular New Comic Opera of Family Quarrels (8)
e.	Monsigny / Corri, Overture to the Deserter (3)
f.	[Piccinni], Overture to lLa Schiava adapted for the Harpsichord or Piano Forte (5)
g.	[Piccinni], Overture to La Buona Figliuola adapted for the Harpsichord or Piano Forte (5)
h.	[Nicolas Dezède], Overture de Blaise et Babet [297-301] (5)
i.	Felice Giardini, The Overture to Astarto for the Harpsichord or Piano Forte (8)
j.	Arne / Domenico Corri, The Soldier Tir’d, A Celebrated Song of Dr. Arne’s Arranged as a Lesson for the Harpsichord [56-58] (3)
k.	J.G.C. Schetky, The Indian Queen, A favorite Strathspey Made into a Rondo for the Piano-Forte (5)
l.	Domenico Corri, OBI, The favorite Air of the Spanish Guitar arranged as a Rondo for the Piano Forte (5)
m.	Cramer, Grand March for the Piano Forte or Harp (7)
n.	T. Latour, The Copenhagen Waltz with Variations for the Piano Forte (5)
o.	M. Holst, Barbara, A Favorite Dance arranged as a Rondo for the Piano Forte (4)
p.	Corri, Dussek (eds.), Original German Waltzen for the Piano Forte or Harpsichord No. I-V (10)
q.	Onorati / Capuzzi, The Favorite Ballet of La Villageoise enlevée ou Les Corsaires (16)

=041  \\$aeng
=100  1\$aStedman, Fabian$d1640-1713$4aut$926734$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7325289
=245  \\$aTintinnalogia. Or The Art of Ringing.$bWherein Is laid down plain and easie Rules for Ringing all sorts of Plain Changes, together with Directions for Pricking and Ringing all Cross Peals; with a full Discovery of the Mystery and Grounds of each Peal
=260  \\$aBath$bKingsmead Reprints$c1970
=300  \\$a136 pages
=500  \\$aFabian Stedman (1640–1713) was an English author and a leading figure in the early history of campanology, particularly in the field of method ringing. He had a key role in publishing two books Tintinnalogia (1668 with Richard Duckworth) and Campanalogia (1677 – written solely by him) which are the first two publications on the subject. He is also regarded as being a pioneer in the branch of mathematics known as Group theory.
=500  \\$aMethod ringing (also known as scientific ringing) is a form of change ringing in which the ringers commit to memory the rules for generating each change of sequence, and pairs of bells are affected. This creates a form of bell music which is continually changing, but which cannot be discerned as a conventional melody. It is a way of sounding continually changing mathematical permutations.

It is distinct from call changes, where the ringers are instructed on how to generate each new change by calls from a conductor, and strictly, only two adjacent bells swap their position at each change.

In method ringing, the ringers are guided from permutation to permutation by following the rules of a method. Ringers typically learn a particular method by studying its "blue line", a diagram which shows its structure.

The underlying mathematical basis of method ringing is intimately linked to group theory. The basic building block of method ringing is plain hunt.

The first method, Grandsire, was designed around 1650, probably by Robert Roan who became master of the College Youths change ringing society in 1652.[1] Details of the method on five bells appeared in print in 1668 in Tintinnalogia (Fabian Stedman with Richard Duckworth) and Campanalogia (1677 – written solely by Stedman), which are the first two publications on the subject.
[https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_ringing]

=500  \\$aAbraham a Sancta Clara (2 July 1644-1 December 1709), German divine, was born at Kreenheinstetten, near Meßkirch. His lay name was Johann Ulrich Megerle. He has been described as "a very eccentric but popular Augustinian monk".
=500  \\$aAmong the types evoked by Abraham a Sancta Clara, there is the "Antiquitet- oder Müntz-Narr", "Bücher-Narr", "Comedi- und Opera-Narr", "Feuerwerck-Narr", "Music Narr", "Nacht Music-Narr", "Tantz-Narr", etc.
=590  \\$aNeu aufgewärmet, und in einer Alapatrit-Pasteten zum Schau-Essen, mit hundert schönen Kupffer-Stichen, zur ehrlichen Ergötzung, und nutzlichen Zeit-Vertreibung, sowohl frölich- als melancholischen Gemüthern aufgesetzt; auch mit einer delicaten Brühe vieler artigen Historien, lustiger Fablen, kurtzweiliger Discursen, und erbaulichen Sitten-Lehren angerichtet.

=300  \\$a81 pages of music$c30 cm
=500  \\$a"Réimpression de l'édition de Paris, 1776"--T.p. verso. This ed. with the original imprint L'Auteur and Le Clerc marchand rue Saint Honoré is dated 1761 in reference sources. The Minkoff reprint date 1976 on the title page could indicate that the present ed. is be a reissue of an earlier Minkoff ed. with that reprint date, however that ed. appears in bibliographic records as a reprint of the 1772 ed.
=590  \\$apour apprendre le doigté de cet instrument, et les différens agrémens dont il est susceptible. Dédiés à Monsieur le Marquis de Rodoüan de Damartin, Mousquetaire de la Seconde Compagnie de la Garde du Roi. Par Mr. l'Abbé le Fils, Ordinaire de l'Académie Royale de Musique. Ces principes sont suivis de deux suites d'airs d'opéra à deux violons, dont le choix lui a paru le meilleur, de plusieurs leçons dans le genre de sonates avec la basse chiffrée pour le clavessin, d'exemples analogues à ces leçons, de préludes dans les tons majeurs et mineurs, et d'une suite de jolis airs variés pour un Violon seul. Les Personnes qui joüent du Par-dessus-de-Viole à quatre cordes peuvent faire usage de ces Principes, en observant seulement de donner aux Lettres t et p une signification contraire à celle que l'on trouvera dans ce Livre.

=245  10$aOorspronk en voortgang der orgelen.$bMet de voortreffelykheid van Alkmaars Groote Orgel
=260  \\$aBuren$bKnuf$c1985$c1727
=300  \\$a1 volume (various pagings)$billustrations$c18 cm
=490  \\$aBibliotheca Organologica$v13
=500  \\$a"The two organs are world-famous. The smaller one, called the "Koororgel" (choir organ), was built in 1511 by Jan van Covelens, and is built against the north wall of the church. It is the oldest playable organ in the Netherlands. The larger organ at the west end of the church is one of the most famous, significant and beautiful organs in the world. It was built by Jacobus Caltus van Hagerbeer, finished in 1645. The magnificent casework, which unusually stretches from floor to vault and makes the organ part of the architecture of the church, was designed by Jacob van Campen, a leading architect of the time. The enormous canvas shutters were painted by Caesar van Everdingen. The organ was rebuilt in 1723 by Frans Caspar Schnitger. He left the casework much as it was, but created an organ in the North German style within the old case. He reused much of the old fluework, but all the mixtures and reeds were new. The organ has not been changed much since then, and is rare in that 90 percent of the original material, pipework, action, soundboards, case, survives. As such it is one of the most important organs in the world." (Wikipedia)

Veldcamps wegens enige perioden tegen hem uitgegeven in het boek genaamd Oorsprong en voortgang der orgelen.' (Alkmaar: K. Mol, 1727)

=500  \\$aDbnl: "Giovanni Antonio Magini, geboren in Padua in 1555 en gestorven in Bologna in 1617, was astronoom, mathematicus en geograaf. In 1588 werd hij aangesteld als hoogleraar in de wiskunde aan de universiteit van Bologna. Hij vervulde deze functie tot zijn dood. In zijn tijd stond hij bekend als een bekwaam astronoom. Hij onderhield contacten met onder andere Tycho Brahe en Johannes Kepler. Zijn astronomische ideeën en geschriften zijn wetenschappelijk gezien desondanks niet van grote betekenis geweest. Zo bleef hij, hoewel hij Copernicus vereerde, een aanhanger van het geocentrische wereldbeeld. Tegenover Galileo stond hij zelfs uitgesproken vijandig. (...)" (https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/_zev001199501_01/_zev001199501_01_0013.php)

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$4aut$aAnonymous$94790
=245  \\$aGründliche Beschreibung der wunderschönen Kirche und des kunstbaren Orgelwerks wie auch des großes Fasses auf dem Kurfürstlichen Residenzhause Gröningen
=250  \\$aReprint
=260  \\$c1695$c1996
=300  \\$a16 pages-xii 
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAm 2. August 1596 versammelten sich in der Kapelle des neu erbauten erzbischöflichen Residenzschlosses zu Gröningen bei Halberstadt 54 der bedeutendsten Organisten aus allen Teilen  Deutschlands, darunter Hans Leo Haßler, Joachim a Burgk und Michael Praetorius. Der Hausherr, Herzog Heinrich Julius von Braunscheig-Lüneburg (1564-1613), postulierter Bischof von Halberstadt, hatte eingeladen, die durch den Halberstädter David Beck 1592 bis 1596 aufgerichtete Orgel zu „probieren“.

Die historische Bedeutung, die der nicht erhalten gebliebene Gröninger Renaissancebau besaß, die 400. Wiederkehr jener denkwürdigen Einweihung der David-Beck-Orgel, aber auch die notwendige Erinnerung an ein Instrument, welches mit den Namen der wegbereitenden Musiktheoretiker Praetorius und Werckmeister unmittelbar verbunden ist, sollte Grund genug sein, einen Nachdruck der „Gründlichen Beschreibung“ vorzulegen.

=245  \\$aNeujahrsblätter der Gesellschaft ab dem Musiksaal:$bTitelblätter 1685-1759
=260  \\$aZürich$bZentralbibliothek$cc. 1993
=300  \\$a[86] pages
=500  \\$aPrint of Mikrofilm AMG Q 332 (Zentralbibliothek Zürch)
=500  \\$aFrom the beginning of the 17th century, various music societies or ‘Collegia musica’ existed in Zurich. Originally strongly supported by the Latin students and teachers, a lot of sacred music was sung there, but instrumental music was also played. The various societies merged several times, as their ‘family tree’ shows:
More and more Zurich music lovers were accepted as new members of the societies, where they had the opportunity to listen to music performed by larger ensembles. From the 18th century at the latest, they were supported by music-loving members of the city's most prestigious families. The societies repeatedly tried to attract professional musicians as members.

=100  \\$4edt$aAlberti, Johann Martin$d1685-1762$924221
=245  \\$aDas vermehrte Schleitzische Gesang-Buch - Anhang unterschiedenier Gebete
=250  \\$a4th ed.
=260  \\$c1727$aSchleiz$bGoderitsch
=300  \\$a2 vols. in one ([xiv]-812-[50] + 144 pages)$bTitle page in red and black ink, engraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aHymnal with Prayerbook
=500  \\$aFirst publication in  1713 by Gottfried Lindner, who had been superintendent in Schleiz since 1708. He also edited the next two editions of 1719 and 1726. After Lindner's death, Johann Martin Alberti became superintendent in 1728. He took over the editing of the hymnal, which was published four times during his time in office until 1761.
=500  \\$aThe hymnal is not only a "singing book", but also a "catechism and teaching book", a "little Bible book", a "wonderful comfort book" and a "complete sermon book"; a hymnal, a catechism and a prayer book belong in the evangelical household, they are often found bound together. The superintendents of Schleiz and Greiz, for example, in the 18th century did not not only compile hymnals, but also prayer books in the same format, collections which had the same format and were published by the same publisher as the corresponding hymnal. These additional books could be books bound to one's own hymnal by the bookbinder. This was possible because the hymnal was not bound.
=500  \\$aIn August 1721, Johann Sebastian Bach gave concerts at Schleiz Castle together with the local court orchestra. 
=501  \\$aBound in with ‘Der gantze Psalter’ and ‘Episteln und Evangelien’
=504  \\$ahttps://www.jstor.org/stable/24237413?seq=1
=590  \\$ain sich haltend die Besten und geistreichsten Lieder des sel. Herrn Lutheri, und vieler andern gottseligen Lieder-Verfasser : Mit vielen Anmerkungen über die fremden oder dunckel-scheinenden Wörter und Redens-Arten wie auch beygefügten Schrifft-Stellen, Nebst einem Anhange gewöhnlicher Kirchen- und enderer Gebete, Gott zu Ehren, vor die allhiesige hoch-Gräfl. Schloss-Kapelle, So dan auch andere Stadt- Land- und Haus-Kirchen, auf hohen Landes-herrschaftl. Befehl ehedem zu dreyen mahlen ausgefertigt von Tit. hrn. Gottfried Lindern, Hoch=Gräfl. Reuß-Pl. hochverordnet=gewesenen Hof=Predigern, Pastore Primario und Superintendenten hieselbst, Jetzo aber zum vierten mahl vermehrter heraus gegeben von Dessen Nachfolger im Amte Johann Martin Alberti

=500  \\$aLeopold Koželuch (1747-1818) was a Czech composer and music teacher. He left around 400 compositions. Koželuch's compositional output included sonatas and concertos for keyboard, the instrument in which he specialised, as well as chamber music, choral music and opera. His substantial output of keyboard compositions reflected the promotion of his reputation as a specialist keyboard virtuoso.

=245  \\$aTwo folders with compositions, arrangements and other musical notes
=500  \\$aA large collection of handwritten music, both original composition and copied music by others, as well as arrangements of songs, etc. 

=500  \\$aDates from 1939 (or earlier) to 1993 (or later).

=500  \\$aPieter Fischer was a musicologist who taught music history at the Conservatory of Amsterdam. He was very interested in art and art history and wrote about 'Bildmotetten'. Fischer was a friend of Gustav Leonhard. Ton Koopman knew him so he bought this set when it came up for auction.

=041  \\$ager$aeng
=100  \\$4cmp$aFroberger, Johann Jacob$d1616-1667$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q60724$914063
=245  \\$aToccaten - Suiten - Lamenti:$bDie Handschrift SA 4450 der Sing-Academie zur Berlin
=250  \\$afacs. ed.
=260  \\$aKassel$bBärenreiter$c2004
=300  \\$axxv-76-55 pages
=490  \\$aDocumenta musicologica$vZweite Reihe: Handschriften-Faksimiles xxxi
=520  \\$aWith manuscript SA 4450 from the music archive of the Sing-Akademie zu Berlin, which was rediscovered in Kiev in 1999 and returned to Berlin in 2001, one of the most important sources on the work of Johann Jacob Froberger (1616-1667) has recently become available to music practitioners and researchers. This magnificent manuscript, presumably made between 1665 and 1670 by the Hamburg organist Johann Kortkamp from autographs, contains a total of 21 authentic compositions by Froberger (six toccatas, thirteen suites and two lamenti). For the majority of the works, the publication offers reliable versions of the music for the first time; in addition, it contains headings, explanations and dedications that have only been handed down here, providing valuable material on Froberger's biography. It is particularly significant that two programmatic compositions by Froberger, previously known only through a brief mention by Johann Mattheson, can now be clearly identified: the "Allemande faite en passant le Rhin" with a detailed description of the musically depicted events and the "Plaincte faite â Londres pour passer la Melancolie" with a revealing autobiographical note about a journey by the composer to England.

The manuscript reproduces a weighty musical monument of significance for scholarship and practice, which is made accessible to a wider circle of interested parties through this representative facsimile edition. The supplementation of the facsimile with a transcription into modern musical notation makes the edition indispensable for practitioners as well.
